## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: population ecology / population dynamics
**Analysis**: This task models the population growth rate dP/dt as a function of population size P and time t, which is the core ODE formulation in population dynamics. Classical models range from exponential and logistic growth to more complex forms with Allee effects, time-dependent carrying capacities, or oscillatory forcing.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Exponential growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (unlimited growth, Malthusian model)
- Logistic growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (density-dependent growth with carrying capacity)
- Gompertz growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (growth decelerating logarithmically near capacity)
- Theta-logistic: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (generalized logistic with shape parameter)
- Logistic with Allee effect: dP_dt = c0 * P * (P - c1) * (1 - c2 * P) (strong Allee effect, growth negative below threshold)
- Weak Allee effect: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 * (1 - c2 * P) (per-capita growth rate increases then decreases with P)
- Beverton-Holt type: dP_dt = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (saturating growth rate)
- Richards growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (flexible sigmoid growth model)
- Time-dependent logistic: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * (1 + c2 * sin(c3 * t)) (seasonal forcing on logistic growth)
- Exponential decay of growth rate: dP_dt = c0 * P * exp(c1 * t) (time-varying intrinsic growth rate)
- Population with harvesting: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 * P (logistic with proportional harvesting)
- Polynomial density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 + c2 * P**3 (higher-order density effects)
- Von Bertalanffy type: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 - c2 * P (anabolic vs catabolic scaling)
- Power-law growth: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 (fractional power growth dynamics)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Negative quadratic term in P (e.g., -c*P^2) indicates density-dependent self-limitation / carrying capacity effects
- Cubic terms in P (e.g., c*P*(P-a)*(K-P)) suggest Allee effects where small populations have negative growth
- Logarithmic dependence on P (e.g., log(K/P)) indicates Gompertz-type asymmetric growth near carrying capacity
- Sinusoidal dependence on time t indicates seasonal or periodic environmental forcing on population dynamics
- Ratio of polynomials in P (e.g., P/(1+cP)) suggests resource competition with handling time or interference
- Product of P with (1 - cP) is the hallmark of logistic regulation where growth vanishes at equilibrium
- Fractional powers of P (e.g., P^(2/3)) suggest surface-area-to-volume scaling in metabolic growth models
- Time appearing only through exponential exp(c*t) suggests a drifting environment or changing intrinsic rate
- Multiple real roots in the growth function of P correspond to multiple equilibria (extinction, Allee threshold, carrying capacity)
